GT Equivalence Verification (CRK30)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

This has three distinct terms:
1. A linear term in A: `-0.25667*A`
2. A term `A*exp(-0.02054*t)` with coefficient `-0.25667`
3. A term `sin(log(A+1))` with coefficient `0.94264`

The key basis functions are: `A`, `A*exp(c*t)`, and `sin(log(A+1))`.

The `sin(log(A+1))` term is highly distinctive - it's a nonlinear oscillatory function of A. Any candidate that doesn't have a mechanism to produce `sin(log(A+1))` cannot match.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of `sin(log(...))` or equivalent:

**Candidates with sin or trigonometric functions:** 
- Candidate 16: `cos(c6*log(c7*Abs(A) + c8*t + 1))` - has `t` inside the log, can't match `sin(log(A+1))` for all t unless c8=0, but then cos vs sin... with phase shift via c6 adjustment? Actually `cos(x) = sin(x + π/2)`, but here there's no additive phase constant inside cos. With c6 as a free constant, `cos(c6*log(...))` ≠ `sin(log(...))` in general since c6 multiplies the argument. If c6=1 and c8=0, we get `cos(log(c7*|A|+1))` which equals `sin(log(c7*|A|+1) + π/2)` - but we need `sin(log(A+1))`, not `sin(log(A+1) + π/2)`. These are different functions. No match.

- Candidate 34: `sin(c6*log(c7*t + 1) + c8)` - this is sin of log(t), not log(A). No match.

**Candidates with log:** 
- Candidate 50: `c5*log(c6*|A| + 1)` - this is `log`, not `sin(log)`. No match.
- Candidate 13: `c3*log(c4*|A| + 1)` with `A^c2` multiplier - not sin(log). No match.

**Candidate 8:** `c3*exp(c4*t)*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6*exp(c7/(c8+t))*log(A*c9 + 1)` - these are `exp*log` terms, not `sin(log)`. No match.

For ALL other candidates, they consist of combinations of: polynomials in A, exponentials in t, rational functions, `Max`, `Abs`, `tanh`, power functions, etc. None of these can produce `sin(log(A+1))`.

The function `sin(log(A+1))` is oscillatory in A (for large A) and cannot be represented by any polynomial, exponential, rational, or other non-trigonometric function. This is a fundamental linear independence argument.

Since no candidate contains a term that can produce `sin(log(A+1))`, and this term has a non-zero coefficient (0.94264), no candidate can match the GT.

Let me verify Candidate 16 more carefully: `c5*cos(c6*log(c7*|A| + c8*t + 1))`. Setting c8=0: `c5*cos(c6*log(c7*|A|+1))`. For A≥0, |A|=A. We need this to equal `0.94264*sin(log(A+1))`. Using `cos(x) = sin(x+π/2)`: `c5*sin(c6*log(c7*A+1) + π/2)`. For this to equal `sin(log(A+1))`, we'd need c6=1, c7=1, and the phase π/2 to vanish - impossible. No match.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically, none contain `sin(log(...))` with A inside, which is required.
